## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (concentration-time rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the central object in chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, approach to equilibrium) and possibly explicit time-dependent rate coefficients (e.g., changing conditions or forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when catalyst/flux is limiting)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- n-th order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general reaction order; c1 can be non-integer empirically)
- Second-order self-reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (dimerization/second-order disappearance in a single-species approximation)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (linear approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with finite capacity: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with depletion/limitation; peak rate at intermediate A)
- Saturating (substrate-limited) disappearance: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate saturates at high A due to finite active sites/transport)
- Product-inhibited / crowding-limited rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate constant decreases with A due to inhibition/viscosity/crowding)
- Time-dependent first-order with exponential drift: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) * A (changing effective rate coefficient over time)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * A (externally modulated kinetics, e.g., light-driven or pulsed conditions)
- Stretched-exponential (distributed-rate) form: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t**c2) (effective slowing due to heterogeneity/aging-like kinetics)
- Mixed-order (intermediate regime): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel pathways: first-order + second-order consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Disappearance of a reactant typically implies dA_dt â‰¤ 0 over most of the trajectory; models often include an overall negative sign multiplying a nonnegative function of A.
- Reaction order inference: if |dA_dt| scales roughly proportional to A, prefer -c*A; if proportional to A**2, prefer -c*A**2; if curvature suggests non-integer order, use -c*A**n.
- Approach to equilibrium behavior (A tends to a plateau) is often captured by dependence on (A - A_eq), e.g., -c*(A-c1); the sign switches around A=c1.
- A rate that increases at low A but decreases at high A (bell-shaped in A) suggests autocatalytic/limited forms like c*A*(c1-A).
- Plateauing of |dA_dt| at high A indicates saturation via rational forms such as -c*A/(c1+A) rather than pure power laws.
- If early-time kinetics are faster/slower than late-time kinetics at the same A, include explicit time dependence in an effective rate coefficient k(t), e.g., (c0 + c1*exp(-c2*t)).
- Observed oscillations or periodic modulation in dA_dt at fixed A suggest an explicitly time-periodic k(t) term like sin(c*t+c0).
- If data show multiple regimes (e.g., initial linear then strongly nonlinear depletion), consider additive pathway models like -c0*A - c1*A**2.

2. `-c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t)` (A times exponential decay in t)

- Term with `A^2/(A^4 + const)` - a rational function of A

Let me check: can `A^2/(c*A^4 + 1)` be expressed as a sum of power functions `A^p`? No - it's a genuine rational function that cannot be decomposed into a finite sum of power-law terms.
